## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate as a function of time and population size, which is a fundamental problem in population ecology. The growth rate dP/dt typically depends on P through density-dependent mechanisms and may depend on t through environmental forcing or time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect, minimum viable population)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (weak Allee effect modification)
- Seasonal exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-varying growth rate with periodicity)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with seasonal forcing)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth curve)
- Exponential decay to capacity: dP_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * P) (constant immigration with density dependence)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-decaying growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence (negative feedback) â†’ multiplicative factor (1 - c*P) or division by (1 + c*P), reflecting resource limitation
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) â†’ additional multiplicative factor (P - c) introducing a lower critical threshold
- Proportionality to population size â†’ dP/dt contains P as a multiplicative factor, since more individuals produce more offspring
- Environmental periodicity â†’ sinusoidal modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) multiplied onto growth terms
- Multiple stable equilibria â†’ cubic or higher-order polynomial in P, creating multiple zero-crossings of dP/dt
- Metabolic scaling â†’ growth terms proportional to P**c with fractional exponent (e.g., P^(3/4) from metabolic theory)
- Harvesting or mortality offset â†’ additive negative constant or negative term independent of P
- Asymmetric growth near capacity â†’ logarithmic terms log(c/P) instead of linear (1 - c*P), as in Gompertz models
